[![Minimum rustc version](https://img.shields.io/badge/rustc-1.63.0+-lightgray.svg)](#rust-version-requirements)\\n7: //!\\n8: //! # PCAP and PCAPNG parsers\\n9: //!\\n10: //! This crate contains several parsers for PCAP and PCAPNG files.\\n11: //!\\n12: //! Compared to other similar projects, it is designed to offer a complete support of the many\\n13: //! possible formats (legacy pcap, pcapng, little or big-endian, etc.) and features (pcapng files\\n14: //! with multiple sections, interfaces, and endianness) while using only safe code and without\\n15: //! copying data (zero-copy).\\n16: //!\\n17: //! The code is available on [Github](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-parser)\\n18: //! and is part of the [Rusticata](https://github.com/rusticata) project.\\n19: //!\\n20: //! # The pcap format(s)\\n21: //!\\n22: //! The [PCAP] format (files usually ending with `.pcap` extension) is rather\\n23: //! trivial. The [PCAPNG] format (usually `.pcapng` extension) is much more complex: it\\n24: //! can be composed of multiple sections, each with multiple interfaces, having\\n25: //! different capture lengths, time precision and even endianness!\\n26: //!\\n27: //! These formats are more containers than data formats: packets contain data,\\n28: //! formatted according to its interface linktype. There are *many* possible\\n29: //! linktypes, defined in the [linktypes registry]. Support for parsing some of\\n30: //! them is provided using the `data` feature (disabled by default).\\n31: //!\\n32: //! This crate provides an abstraction over these different formats.\\n33: //!\\n34: //! [PCAP]: https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat\\n35: //! [PCAPNG]: https://pcapng.github.io/pcapng/\\n36: //! [linktypes registry]: https://www.tcpdump.org/linktypes.html\\n37: //!\\n38: //! # Parsing a file\\n39: //!\\n40: //! `pcap-parser` provides several ways of parsing pcap data. Choosing the right\\n41: //! one is mostly driven by resources: if the input file is small, the\\n42: //! `parse_pcap` and `parse_pcapng` functions can be used directly.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! Fine-grained functions are also available, to parse specifically some block\\n45: //! types for example. They are listed in the `pcap` and `pcapng` modules.\\n46: //!\\n47: //! If the input is larger and cannot fit into memory, then streaming parsers\\n48: //! are available. They work by iterating on blocks, and so do not require to map\\n49: //! the entire input. They cannot seek to a specific block, however.\\n50: //!\\n51: //! *Note: due to PCAPNG limitations, it is not possible to directly seek in\\n52: //! a file to get a packet and handle it: the caller has to iterate though the\\n53: //! file and store (at least) the interface descriptions for the current\\n54: //! section, in order of appearance.*\\n55: //!\\n56: //! ## Example: streaming parsers\\n57: //!\\n58: //! The following code shows how to parse a file in the pcap-ng format, using a\\n59: //! [`PcapNGReader`] streaming parser.\\n60: //! This reader provides a convenient abstraction over the file format, and takes\\n61: //! care of the endianness.\\n62: //!\\n63: //! ```rust\\n64: //! use pcap_parser::*;\\n65: //! use pcap_parser::traits::PcapReaderIterator;\\n66: //! use std::fs::File;\\n67: //!\\n68: //! # let path = \\\"assets/test001-le.pcapng\\\";\\n69: //! let file = File::open(path).unwrap();\\n70: //! let mut num_blocks = 0;\\n71: //! let mut reader = PcapNGReader::new(65536, file).expect(\\\"PcapNGReader\\\");\\n72: //! loop {\\n73: //!     match reader.next() {\\n74: //!         Ok((offset, _block)) => {\\n75: //!             println!(\\\"got new block\\\");\\n76: //!             num_blocks += 1;\\n77: //!             reader.consume(offset);\\n78: //!         },\\n79: //!         Err(PcapError::Eof) => break,\\n80: //!         Err(PcapError::Incomplete(_)) => {\\n81: //!             reader.refill().unwrap();\\n82: //!         },\\n83: //!         Err(e) => panic!(\\\"error while reading: {:?}\\\", e),\\n84: //!     }\\n85: //! }\\n86: //! println!(\\\"num_blocks: {}\\\", num_blocks);\\n87: //! ```\\n88: //! See [`PcapNGReader`] for a complete example,\\n89: //! including handling of linktype and accessing packet data.\\n90: //!\\n91: //! See also the [`pcapng`] module for more details about the new capture file format.\\n92: //!\\n93: //! For legacy pcap files, use similar code with the\\n94: //! [`LegacyPcapReader`] streaming parser.\\n95: //!\\n96: //! See [pcap-analyzer](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer), in particular the\\n97: //! [libpcap-tools](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/libpcap-tools) and\\n98: //! [pcap-info](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/pcap-info) modules\\n99: //! for more examples.\\n100: //!\\n101: //! ## Example: generic streaming parsing\\n102: //!\\n103: //! To create a pcap reader for input in either PCAP or PCAPNG format, use the\\n104: //! [`create_reader`] function.\\n105: //!\\n106: //! # Serialization\\n107: //!\\n108: //! Support for serialization (*i.e.* generating binary data) is available by\\n109: //! enabling the `serialize` feature.\\n110: //! Most structures gain the `to_vec()` method (provided by the `ToVec` trait).\\n111: //!\\n112: //! Note: support is still experimental, though working. API may change in the\\n113: //! future.\\n114: \\n115: #![deny(/*missing_docs,*/\\n116:         unstable_features,\\n117:         unused_import_braces, unused_qualifications)]\\n118: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\\n119: #![allow(clippy::upper_case_acronyms)]\\n120: // pragmas for doc\\n121: #![deny(rustdoc::broken_intra_doc_links)]\\n122: #![cfg_attr(docsrs, feature(doc_cfg))]\\n123: #![doc(test(\\n124:     no_crate_inject,\\n125:     attr(deny(warnings/*, rust_2018_idioms*/), allow(dead_code, unused_variables))\\n126: ))]\\n127: \\n128: mod utils;\\n129: pub use utils::{Data, MutableData};\\n130: \\n131: mod blocks;\\n132: mod capture;\\n133: mod endianness;\\n134: mod error;\\n135: mod linktype;\\n136: pub use blocks::*;\\n137: pub use capture::*;\\n138: pub use error::*;\\n139: pub use linktype::*;\\n140: \\n141: pub mod pcap;\\n142: pub mod pcapng;\\n143: pub use pcap::*;\\n144: pub use pcapng::*;\\n145: \\n146: pub mod traits;\\n147: \\n148: #[cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")]\\n149: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")))]\\n150: mod serialize;\\n151: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")))]\\n152: #[cfg(feature = \\\"serialize\\\")]\\n153: pub use serialize::ToVec;\\n154: \\n155: #[cfg(feature = \\\"data\\\")]\\n156: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \\\"data\\\")))]\\n157: pub mod data;\\n158: \\n159: // re-exports\\n160: pub use nom;\\n161: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/pcap-parser--dibench@7fc73b8e4b0b5a0a54b3caeeec206b69d55b4ec3/-/blob/src/lib.rs\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f4347c25-26c7-4421-83e9-53f9529de9bf","uuid":"da912fe7-3171-4f48-b6ac-3306c90d7b58","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! [![Minimum rustc version](https://img.shields.io/badge/rustc-1.63.0+-lightgray.svg)](#rust-version-requirements)\n7: //!\n8: //! # PCAP and PCAPNG parsers\n9: //!\n10: //! This crate contains several parsers for PCAP and PCAPNG files.\n11: //!\n12: //! Compared to other similar projects, it is designed to offer a complete support of the many\n13: //! possible formats (legacy pcap, pcapng, little or big-endian, etc.) and features (pcapng files\n14: //! with multiple sections, interfaces, and endianness) while using only safe code and without\n15: //! copying data (zero-copy).\n16: //!\n17: //! The code is available on [Github](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-parser)\n18: //! and is part of the [Rusticata](https://github.com/rusticata) project.\n19: //!\n20: //! # The pcap format(s)\n21: //!\n22: //! The [PCAP] format (files usually ending with `.pcap` extension) is rather\n23: //! trivial. The [PCAPNG] format (usually `.pcapng` extension) is much more complex: it\n24: //! can be composed of multiple sections, each with multiple interfaces, having\n25: //! different capture lengths, time precision and even endianness!\n26: //!\n27: //! These formats are more containers than data formats: packets contain data,\n28: //! formatted according to its interface linktype. There are *many* possible\n29: //! linktypes, defined in the [linktypes registry]. Support for parsing some of\n30: //! them is provided using the `data` feature (disabled by default).\n31: //!\n32: //! This crate provides an abstraction over these different formats.\n33: //!\n34: //! [PCAP]: https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat\n35: //! [PCAPNG]: https://pcapng.github.io/pcapng/\n36: //! [linktypes registry]: https://www.tcpdump.org/linktypes.html\n37: //!\n38: //! # Parsing a file\n39: //!\n40: //! `pcap-parser` provides several ways of parsing pcap data. Choosing the right\n41: //! one is mostly driven by resources: if the input file is small, the\n42: //! `parse_pcap` and `parse_pcapng` functions can be used directly.\n43: //!\n44: //! Fine-grained functions are also available, to parse specifically some block\n45: //! types for example. They are listed in the `pcap` and `pcapng` modules.\n46: //!\n47: //! If the input is larger and cannot fit into memory, then streaming parsers\n48: //! are available. They work by iterating on blocks, and so do not require to map\n49: //! the entire input. They cannot seek to a specific block, however.\n50: //!\n51: //! *Note: due to PCAPNG limitations, it is not possible to directly seek in\n52: //! a file to get a packet and handle it: the caller has to iterate though the\n53: //! file and store (at least) the interface descriptions for the current\n54: //! section, in order of appearance.*\n55: //!\n56: //! ## Example: streaming parsers\n57: //!\n58: //! The following code shows how to parse a file in the pcap-ng format, using a\n59: //! [`PcapNGReader`] streaming parser.\n60: //! This reader provides a convenient abstraction over the file format, and takes\n61: //! care of the endianness.\n62: //!\n63: //! ```rust\n64: //! use pcap_parser::*;\n65: //! use pcap_parser::traits::PcapReaderIterator;\n66: //! use std::fs::File;\n67: //!\n68: //! # let path = \"assets/test001-le.pcapng\";\n69: //! let file = File::open(path).unwrap();\n70: //! let mut num_blocks = 0;\n71: //! let mut reader = PcapNGReader::new(65536, file).expect(\"PcapNGReader\");\n72: //! loop {\n73: //!     match reader.next() {\n74: //!         Ok((offset, _block)) => {\n75: //!             println!(\"got new block\");\n76: //!             num_blocks += 1;\n77: //!             reader.consume(offset);\n78: //!         },\n79: //!         Err(PcapError::Eof) => break,\n80: //!         Err(PcapError::Incomplete(_)) => {\n81: //!             reader.refill().unwrap();\n82: //!         },\n83: //!         Err(e) => panic!(\"error while reading: {:?}\", e),\n84: //!     }\n85: //! }\n86: //! println!(\"num_blocks: {}\", num_blocks);\n87: //! ```\n88: //! See [`PcapNGReader`] for a complete example,\n89: //! including handling of linktype and accessing packet data.\n90: //!\n91: //! See also the [`pcapng`] module for more details about the new capture file format.\n92: //!\n93: //! For legacy pcap files, use similar code with the\n94: //! [`LegacyPcapReader`] streaming parser.\n95: //!\n96: //! See [pcap-analyzer](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer), in particular the\n97: //! [libpcap-tools](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/libpcap-tools) and\n98: //! [pcap-info](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/pcap-info) modules\n99: //! for more examples.\n100: //!\n101: //! ## Example: generic streaming parsing\n102: //!\n103: //! To create a pcap reader for input in either PCAP or PCAPNG format, use the\n104: //! [`create_reader`] function.\n105: //!\n106: //! # Serialization\n107: //!\n108: //! Support for serialization (*i.e.* generating binary data) is available by\n109: //! enabling the `serialize` feature.\n110: //! Most structures gain the `to_vec()` method (provided by the `ToVec` trait).\n111: //!\n112: //! Note: support is still experimental, though working. API may change in the\n113: //! future.\n114: \n115: #![deny(/*missing_docs,*/\n116:         unstable_features,\n117:         unused_import_braces, unused_qualifications)]\n118: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\n119: #![allow(clippy::upper_case_acronyms)]\n120: // pragmas for doc\n121: #![deny(rustdoc::broken_intra_doc_links)]\n122: #![cfg_attr(docsrs, feature(doc_cfg))]\n123: #![doc(test(\n124:     no_crate_inject,\n125:     attr(deny(warnings/*, rust_2018_idioms*/), allow(dead_code, unused_variables))\n126: ))]\n127: \n128: mod utils;\n129: pub use utils::{Data, MutableData};\n130: \n131: mod blocks;\n132: mod capture;\n133: mod endianness;\n134: mod error;\n135: mod linktype;\n136: pub use blocks::*;\n137: pub use capture::*;\n138: pub use error::*;\n139: pub use linktype::*;\n140: \n141: pub mod pcap;\n142: pub mod pcapng;\n143: pub use pcap::*;\n144: pub use pcapng::*;\n145: \n146: pub mod traits;\n147: \n148: #[cfg(feature = \"serialize\")]\n149: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \"serialize\")))]\n150: mod serialize;\n151: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \"serialize\")))]\n152: #[cfg(feature = \"serialize\")]\n153: pub use serialize::ToVec;\n154: \n155: #[cfg(feature = \"data\")]\n156: #[cfg_attr(docsrs, doc(cfg(feature = \"data\")))]\n157: pub mod data;\n158: \n159: // re-exports\n160: pub use nom;\n161: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/pcap-parser--dibench@7fc73b8e4b0b5a0a54b3caeeec206b69d55b4ec3/-/blob/src/lib.rs"}}}

The [PCAPNG] format (usually `.pcapng` extension) is much more complex: it\n    26→can be composed of multiple sections, each with multiple interfaces, having\n    27→different capture lengths, time precision and even endianness!\n    28→\n    29→These formats are more containers than data formats: packets contain data,\n    30→formatted according to its interface linktype. There are *many* possible\n    31→linktypes, defined in the [linktypes registry]. Support for parsing some of\n    32→them is provided using the `data` feature (disabled by default).\n    33→\n    34→This crate provides an abstraction over these different formats.\n    35→\n    36→[PCAP]: https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat\n    37→[PCAPNG]: https://pcapng.github.io/pcapng/\n    38→[linktypes registry]: https://www.tcpdump.org/linktypes.html\n    39→\n    40→# Parsing a file\n    41→\n    42→`pcap-parser` provides several ways of parsing pcap data. Choosing the right\n    43→one is mostly driven by resources: if the input file is small, the\n    44→`parse_pcap` and `parse_pcapng` functions can be used directly.\n    45→\n    46→Fine-grained functions are also available, to parse specifically some block\n    47→types for example. They are listed in the `pcap` and `pcapng` modules.\n    48→\n    49→If the input is larger and cannot fit into memory, then streaming parsers\n    50→are available. They work by iterating on blocks, and so do not require to map\n    51→the entire input. They cannot seek to a specific block, however.\n    52→\n    53→*Note: due to PCAPNG limitations, it is not possible to directly seek in\n    54→a file to get a packet and handle it: the caller has to iterate though the\n    55→file and store (at least) the interface descriptions for the current\n    56→section, in order of appearance.*\n    57→\n    58→## Example: streaming parsers\n    59→\n    60→The following code shows how to parse a file in the pcap-ng format, using a\n    61→[`PcapNGReader`] streaming parser.\n    62→This reader provides a convenient abstraction over the file format, reading: {:?}\", e),\n    85→    }\n    86→}\n    87→println!(\"num_blocks: {}\", num_blocks);\n    88→```\n    89→See [`PcapNGReader`] for a complete example,\n    90→including handling of linktype and accessing packet data.\n    91→\n    92→See also the [`pcapng`] module for more details about the new capture file format.\n    93→\n    94→For legacy pcap files, use similar code with the\n The [PCAPNG] format (usually `.pcapng` extension) is much more complex: it\ncan be composed of multiple sections, each with multiple interfaces, having\ndifferent capture lengths, time precision and even endianness!\n\nThese formats are more containers than data formats: packets contain data,\nformatted according to its interface linktype. There are *many* possible\nlinktypes, defined in the [linktypes registry]. Support for parsing some of\nthem is provided using the `data` feature (disabled by default).\n\nThis crate provides an abstraction over these different formats.\n\n[PCAP]: https://wiki.wireshark.org/Development/LibpcapFileFormat\n[PCAPNG]: https://pcapng.github.io/pcapng/\n[linktypes registry]: https://www.tcpdump.org/linktypes.html\n\n# Parsing a file\n\n`pcap-parser` provides several ways of parsing pcap data. Choosing the right\none is mostly driven by resources: if the input file is small, the\n`parse_pcap` and `parse_pcapng` functions can be used directly.\n\nFine-grained functions are also available, to parse specifically some block\ntypes for example. They are listed in the `pcap` and `pcapng` modules.\n\nIf the input is larger and cannot fit into memory, then streaming parsers\nare available. They work by iterating on blocks, and so do not require to map\nthe entire input. They cannot seek to a specific block, however.\n\n*Note: due to PCAPNG limitations, it is not possible to directly seek in\na file to get a packet and handle it: the caller has to iterate though the\nfile and store (at least) the interface descriptions for the current\nsection, in order of appearance.*\n\n## Example: streaming parsers\n\nThe following code shows how to parse a file in the pcap-ng format, using a\n[`PcapNGReader`] streaming parser.\nThis reader provides a convenient abstraction over the file format, and takes\ncare of the endianness.\n\n```rust\nuse pcap_parser::*;\nuse pcap_parser::traits::PcapReaderIterator;\nuse std::fs::File;\n\nlet file = File::open(path).unwrap();\nlet mut num_blocks = 0;\nlet mut reader = PcapNGReader::new(65536, file).expect(\"PcapNGReader\");\nloop {\n    match reader.next() {\n        Ok((offset, _block)) => {\n            println!(\"got new block\");\n            num_blocks += 1;\n            reader.consume(offset);\n        },\n        Err(PcapError::Eof) => break,\n        Err(PcapError::Incomplete(_)) => {\n            reader.refill().unwrap();\n        },\n        Err(e) => panic!(\"error while reading: {:?}\", e),\n    }\n}\nprintln!(\"num_blocks: {}\", num_blocks);\n```\nSee [`PcapNGReader`] for a complete example,\nincluding handling of linktype and accessing packet data.\n\nSee also the [`pcapng`] module for more details about the new capture file format.\n\nFor legacy pcap files, use similar code with the\n[`LegacyPcapReader`] streaming parser.\n\nSee [pcap-analyzer](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer), in particular the\n[libpcap-tools](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/libpcap-tools) and\n[pcap-info](https://github.com/rusticata/pcap-analyzer/tree/master/pcap-info) modules\nfor more examples.","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":138}}}
